["TATTOO REMOVAL FAQs:" "b"]
["" "b"]
["How does laser tattoo removal work?" "b"]
["The laser light is passed over the tattooed skin, microscopically shattering the pigment into tiny particles which are more easily processed and eliminated by the body.  Most patients undergo a series of 10 minute treatments.  A mild to moderate irritation of the overlying skin is to be expected for a few days to a week, depending on the depth and amount of pigment to be removed." "b"]
["" "b"]
["Who performs the procedures?  Our physicians, physician assistants and registered nurses have been extensively trained on tattoo removal." "b"]
["" "b"]
["Can all colors be removed?  Most colors can be removed completely.  Some colors may require more treatments than others." "b"]
["" "b"]
["How many treatments will I need?  Tattoo removal requires multiple treatments spaced 4-8 weeks apart.  There are several different factors involved in determining how many treatments your particular tattoo will need." "b"]
["" "b"]
["Does it hurt?  There is a minimal amount of discomfort involved in this procedure. Most patients require an anesthetic cream to be applied 30 minutes before the procedure.  As we treat the area, we cool the overlying skin with a skin cooling device.  This combination of topical anesthesia and cooling air makes the procedure as comfortable as possible." "b"]

[">>>> box - though more for exercise and not at all competitively, used to" "b"]
[">>>> wrestle, done a fair amount of pushing with my training partner." "b"]
[">>>>" "b"]
[">>>> I've heard that Aikido is terrible as a self-defense technique, but" "b"]
[">>>> totally unmatched for embodied cognition work. Knowing how to fall, keep" "b"]
[">>>> your balance, use the opponents energy etc etc.  A friend/acquaintance of" "b"]
[">>>> mine studies flow and peak performance for a living and swears its the most" "b"]
[">>>> generally useful movement practice for tuning the mind." "b"]
[">>>>" "b"]
[">>>> If anyone on the list has Aikido recs, or is interested in joining a" "b"]
[">>>> gym together, I'd be more inclined to do the work of finding a good teacher" "b"]
[">>>> if I knew it would benefit others as well." "b"]
[">>>>" "b"]
[">>> On Mon, Jul 6, 2015 at 9:33 PM, Eli Tyre <eli...@gmail.com> wrote:" "h"]

[">>> I'm in the Bay Area for the Summer from Chicago, and I'm feeling the" "b"]
[">>>>> lack of my regular martial arts partner." "b"]
[">>>>>" "b"]
[">>>>> I'm looking for 1) recommendations for instructors or schools and 2)" "b"]
[">>>>> people who might want to spar or push (sort of like sparing, but with an" "b"]
[">>>>> emphasis on feeling and taking your opponents balance, at varying levels of" "b"]
[">>>>> speed and force) with me on a regular basis." "b"]
[">>>>>" "b"]
[">>>>> In general, I'm interested in internal martial arts as long as there" "b"]
[">>>>> is a strong component of actually sparring. Most recently, I've been" "b"]
[">>>>> practicing Yi Quan <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yiquan>, and I'd" "b"]
[">>>>> like to continue with that, but I've also done a little Bagua, which I am" "b"]
[">>>>> also very interested in. That said, good instructors and consistent" "b"]
[">>>>> practice partners outweigh preferences of style and I'm open to suggestions." "b"]

["To unsubscribe from this group and stop receiving emails from it, send an email to overcomingbiasnyc+unsubscribe@googlegroups.com." "b"]

["Groping for a better way here is basically a complex systems issue." "b"]
["" "b"]
["I have dealt with a whole lot of complex systems issues in my life, and" "b"]
["also seen a number of times how conundra which seemed unsolvable really are" "b"]
["solvable, if one is clear and persistent enough, and avoids falling into" "b"]
["traps which are basically silly if one reflects a bit. Does this say we" "b"]
["need always to remember the practice of reflection, and" "b"]
["that we need to jump a meta level and ask what we are really assuming here?" "b"]
["" "b"]
["Several examples, first one on the table now:" "b"]
["" "b"]
["On Sat, Jun 4, 2016 at 2:13 AM, Kelly Starks KellySt@aol.com" "h"]
["[lifeboatfoundation] <lifeboatfoundation@yahoogroups.com> wrote:" "h"]
[">" "b"]
[">" "b"]
["> Really, I'ld much more recommend focused groups on individual issues," "b"]
["> rather then sweeping everything groups. The layer temd to lose focus, and" "b"]
["> member support with so many contradictory issues fighting for attention." "b"]
["> They also never get a very deep grasp of any of the individual issues." "b"]
[">" "b"]
["> Many, many people have pursued exactly this common sense reaction/solution" "b"]
["to any kind of complexity." "b"]
["" "b"]
["One name for it is \"stovepiping\"." "b"]
["" "b"]
["Ironically, I am guilty of a bit of that myself the past few weeks. Just" "b"]
["pick a target small enough that I can understand it and not be in perpetual" "b"]
["angst, and push hard on something I can understand without further deep" "b"]
["thinking about my goals. These few weeks, it happens to be trying to use" "b"]
["time-stamped 40khz data on deep brain recordings, to figure out what clock" "b"]
["times to use for further analysis. BUT: I have NOT committed to spending" "b"]
["the rest of my life on that, or renouncing my continuing interest in larger" "b"]
["life-0or-death issues which no fully sane person would ever hide from." "b"]
["" "b"]
["There are times when I wonder whether the superior growth in REAL economic" "b"]
["productivity in the 1960s was due as much to Walt Disney cartoons and" "b"]
["films, versus what a lot of people are picking up from teh media today." "b"]
["Kids of my generation were very familiar with that silly ostrich character" "b"]
["who would try to solve all his problems by burying his head in the sand." "b"]
["People have voted for a lot of that lately. NOT EVERYONE should spend more" "b"]
["than, say, 10% of his or her time thinking about the big picture, BUT IF we" "b"]
["enforce a homogeneous culture and society which prevents ANY serious" "b"]
["organized group from trying to figure it out..." "b"]
["" "b"]
["Well, not being conscious of a problem is a predictable way of never" "b"]
["solving it, in the world of complex systems like this." "b"]
["" "b"]
["There are ever so many examples of stovepipes, and in recent years.. any" "b"]
["success?" "b"]
["" "b"]
["A REAL example of success versus stovepiping... needs some buildup, sorry." "b"]
["" "b"]
["Limited though it is, and more though there is which still needs to be" "b"]
["done,  the restructuring of the US electric power system since Ronald" "b"]
["Reagan, is one interesting example of a success. Maybe it would be useful" "b"]
["to think of the attitudes and assumptions which made success possible, and" "b"]
["are very very different form most of what we see in the world today. (I" "b"]
["would say different form what we see in other sectors... except that there" "b"]
["are sectors of electric power woefully caught in the same old kind of" "b"]
["morass.)" "b"]
["" "b"]
["It started with a certain kind of vision. The vision is that markets," "b"]
["responding directly to what consumers want, can be more effective and lead" "b"]
["to faster growth than political mechanisms, from laws to regulations to" "b"]
["stakeholder sessions divvying up loot. Reagan admitted that the purest of" "b"]
["government-free market ideas hadn't ever really worked in this sector, and" "b"]
["couldn't, because of \"natural monopoly.\" But \"natural monopoly\" was only" "b"]
["for transmission and distribution, not for generation. So let's deregulate" "b"]
["generation, let's separate it from ownership of the wires, and let's design" "b"]
["a market to replace the old political systems." "b"]
["" "b"]
["Already a few more general principles emerge, one of which is \"market" "b"]
["design.\" While naive and uneducated people gravitate naturally towards the" "b"]
["simple extremes of total government or stakeholder rule, versus the kind of" "b"]
["markets they had in the dark ages (free competition of tribes of wandering" "b"]
["bandits, uninhibited by law or fairness), there are folks who have come to" "b"]
["understand that market design is a very serious business. Maybe we need" "b"]
["more of that understanding in the world as a whole. In a way, there is an" "b"]
["analogy between designing a market and designing a poll" "b"]
["or panel session which more effectively draws out the real preferences and" "b"]
["beliefs of the client audience, the people to be served. (And yes, while" "b"]
["customers come to mind first, there is are imported limited roles for other" "b"]
["roles.)" "b"]
["" "b"]
["When people started trying to implement Reagan's policy, there were..." "b"]
["politely... some growing pains. Enron was the least of them. I had a lot of" "b"]
["contact until about a year ago with the leading power engineers (a diverse" "b"]
["group in themselves), and they were aghast at the crude ideological" "b"]
["bunglers who came in, like a bull in the China shop, and really broke a lot" "b"]
["of stuff. Those memories have not gone away. But I also remember a woman" "b"]
["who played a lead role in the community.. who worked hard to bridge the" "b"]
["gap. It WAS bridged, not only by her but by others seeing the same vision.." "b"]
["and the system now is very, very different, and better really, than it was" "b"]
["before Reagan. (Naturally, I don't support all of Reagan's ideas. Some I" "b"]
["abhor.  Yet many of the worst evils committed by conservatives today are in" "b"]
["fact bits of corruption and hypocrisy they inserted through a kind of group" "b"]
["self-interest effects.)" "b"]
["" "b"]
["One of the steps in her success... was convening a workshop under White" "b"]
["House authority, at the White House conference center (years after Reagan" "b"]
["was gone and the system was still in disequilibrium), bringing together top" "b"]
["serious market economists and top systems-level power engineers and policy" "b"]
["thinkers." "b"]
["" "b"]
["At that workshop, I still remember when one of the top economists said:\"You" "b"]
["power engineers need to get past the trees, and see the forest. What we" "b"]
["have here is basically just a simple problem of supply and demand. What" "b"]
["really matters here are that we have customers, consumers at the end of the" "b"]
["line, who consume electricity, and producers, who produce the electricity." "b"]
["All that maters is that we understand the two, and make connections. Demand" "b"]
["at the end, and supply at the start. What else is there?\"" "b"]
["" "b"]
["It was so amazing to see the varied expressions on the faces of the power" "b"]
["engineers. (I hope my own smile did not come off like a smirk.)" "b"]
["" "b"]
["\"Well, between the two, there is simply the biggest machine ever built by" "b"]
["humans, one giant machine which cost trillions of dollars to build, the" "b"]
["power grid itself, the actual physical system which makes those connections" "b"]
["in the real world.\"" "b"]
["" "b"]
["Gradually, people realized more and more than lack of communication across" "b"]
["disciplines, aka stovepiping, really was at the core of why people had" "b"]
["floundered endlessly. We needed to mode towards working, concrete designs" "b"]
["which satisfy the filters and the highest understanding of more than one" "b"]
["discipline at once." "b"]
["" "b"]
["The economists were rightly frustrated when they probed to find what kind" "b"]
["of engineers, specifically, needed to be involved.   Somehow the talk went" "b"]
["to civil engineering for awhile, and engineers informed the economists that" "b"]
["there are big divides (\"stovepipes\") even between bridge people versus road" "b"]
["people, let alone railroad people, and building people. Stovepiping tends" "b"]
["to be fractal. When you divide the realm up into two parts to make it more" "b"]
["tractible, you end up dividing the halves in half, and so on. Practical" "b"]
["people in high levels of industry know very well the saying about \"knowing" "b"]
["more and more about less and less, until you know everything about nothing.\"" "b"]
["" "b"]
["To get past useless bullshit of all kinds, and generate real product and" "b"]
["workable designs, places like NSF and EPRI led the development of new" "b"]
["crossdisciplinary teams. In fact, the calls for proposals from those places" "b"]
["were themselves a kind of exercise in rational, open competitive market" "b"]
["design! (I can't help thinking of one leading electricity economist who" "b"]
["wanted even more formal game-theoretic structure, even as one of his" "b"]
["collaborators snuck out to a Congressman friend to eliminate competition" "b"]
["altogether.)" "b"]
["" "b"]
["The issue of stovepiping is really just a shallow surface-level reflection" "b"]
["of a deeper issue in intelligent systems, which, by definition, are systems" "b"]
["intended to cope well with incredibly complex flows of information and" "b"]
["decision challenges." "b"]
["In neural networks, even a novice would be appalled by the idea that ALL" "b"]
["neurons should either be FULLY connected in practice with all other" "b"]
["neurons, or -- even worse -- split up into disconnected heaps. Or even a" "b"]
["red army style of hierarchy, which does not work so well in organizing" "b"]
["economic activity. (Terrorizing people in Iraq and Syria is a different" "b"]
["matter, for later discussion.) A web of connection is what's needed." "b"]
["" "b"]
["===========" "b"]
["" "b"]
["And so... if we agree that the extinction of the human species is a serious" "b"]
["issue, we need SOME serious venues for not putting our heads in the sand," "b"]
["for saying \"the buck stops here\" (intellectually), and doing what we can," "b"]
["bit by bit, to try to wrestle with the issue of how to stay alive." "b"]
["" "b"]
["" "b"]
["------------------" "b"]
["" "b"]
["That's all pretty basic. Ben and Jens want us now to go ahead and engage." "b"]
["" "b"]
["I don't see the threats to our liberty as one of the big three-or-four" "b"]
["DIRECT threats of human extinction" "b"]
["(which I still see as NUC/H2S/AI/(bio)), but when I look to any of the" "b"]
["concrete things we COULD do to reduce the probability of extinction, I see" "b"]
["the growth of authoritarian and corrupt cultures as an overwhelming barrier" "b"]
["at present." "b"]
["Without the free market place of ideas -- more important in the end than" "b"]
["the market place for goods -- I see little hope," "b"]
["for example, for crucial new technologies which I know about very well," "b"]
["THANKS in great part to what I got from the" "b"]
["open competitive system we used to have at NSF. (No, I am not saying it is" "b"]
["100% gone yet, but... a lot has happened in the past few years, at many" "b"]
["agencies.)" "b"]
["" "b"]
["Last Sunday, at Quakers, one of the weighty (also active and young by my" "b"]
["standards) Quakes spoke about a \"bad seed\" which somehow seems to have been" "b"]
["carried on the wind... which is now threatening our very most basic" "b"]
["freedoms, and constitutional rights, and needs to be taken very, very" "b"]
["seriously. He was totally nonpartisan in what he said, but at afterthought" "b"]
["time, a wiccan outlier member of the meeting said: \"But when we discuss" "b"]
["these things" "b"]
["in Meeting proper, we need to be very vigilant to be sure we are echoing" "b"]
["the spirit and not just our own thoughts, which may be biased and" "b"]
["partisan.\" Several people had spoken (much more than usual) after he spoke," "b"]
["and perhaps some were reactive, but the initial speaker then gently said..." "b"]
["there is nothing partisan about this,. He mentioned several issues" "b"]
["involving inspectors general at some agencies, which really involve the" "b"]
["rule of law as such. I quietly thought of several other examples. In truth," "b"]
["I even believe -- whatever Hillary's many obvious limitations -- that the" "b"]
["IG+FBI investigation of her emails should be seen as much more of a scandal" "b"]
["about the investigators than about her," "b"]
["and that failure to appreciate ... the more general cancer... could be" "b"]
["fatal in the end. It is not personal or partisan." "b"]
["" "b"]
["Of course, to Quakers, subordinating the US constitution either to sharia" "b"]
["or to canon law would be equally repugnant, and brings back memories of how" "b"]
["it used to be. He tweaked my conscience just as much as Jens did." "b"]
["" "b"]
["==============================" "b"]
["" "b"]
["Well, Jens and Ben, I still haven't directly addressed your questions. I" "b"]
["apologize." "b"]
["But at least I agree that we should try." "b"]

["March With Scott at Pride" "b"]

["I've been marching in the San Francisco Pride Parade for 20 years, and each year our community moves one step closer towards full equality. This year is no exception. While the LGBTQ community has advanced tremendously on issues like marriage equality, healthcare access, and parental rights, we are now confronted by a reactionary backlash from those who would seek to undo that for which we have fought so hard. States like North Carolina and Mississippi are mounting vigorous, last-ditch campaigns to allow LGBTQ discrimination to run rampant under the guise of religious freedom. We cannot afford to let our guard down now." "b"]
["" "b"]

And while we have much work left to be done before we can declare “mission accomplished,” let’s take a moment to celebrate what we have achieved together. On June 26, I ask that you join one of the largest pride parades in the world and march in my contingent once again. If you are interested, please RSVP here  <http://www.scottwiener.com/sf_pride?utm_campaign=pride2016&utm_medium=email&utm_source=scottwiener>and email Jason Galisatus <mailto:jgalisatus@gmail.com> with any questions you may have. ["POLICY WORK" "b"]
["" "b"]
["Paid Parental Leave: Guaranteeing Fully Paid Leave for New Parents" "b"]
["In April, Mayor Lee signed my legislation making San Francisco the first place in the United States to guarantee fully paid parental leave to new parents. Our country’s parental leave policies are woefully behind the rest of the world. We shouldn’t be forcing new mothers and fathers to choose between spending precious bonding time with their children and putting food on the table <http://www.huffingtonpost.com/scott-wiener/fighting-for-full-paid-parental-leave_b_9612534.html>. Under current California law, employees taking parental leave receive 55% of their wages for six weeks through state disability. My legislation, which the Board of Supervisors unanimously passed <http://www.nytimes.com/2016/04/06/us/san-francisco-approves-fully-paid-parental-leave.html>, requires that employers pay their employees the remaining balance of their income, so that for up to six weeks of leave the employee will receive his or her full wages. The legislation applies to both parents and to both births and adoptions.  I’m proud San Francisco is once again taking the lead in putting our workers and our families first, and I hope the state and country follow <http://www.nytimes.com/2016/04/07/us/why-parental-leave-policies-are-changing.html?_r=0> and provide more comprehensive parental leave programs. I want to thank my aide, Andres Power <http://www.theguardian.com/us-news/2016/apr/08/paid-parental-leave-san-francisco-new-law-scott-wiener>, who was instrumental in crafting this legislation, and is now out for his own parental leave." "b"]
["" "b"]
["" "b"]
["" "b"]
["" "b"]
["Mayor Lee signing Scott's Paid Parental Leave law at the San Francisco Public Library." "b"]
["" "b"]
["Better Roofs Ordinance: Requiring Solar Panels on New Construction" "b"]
["" "b"]
["To fight climate change and achieve a clean energy future, we need to take decisive steps to reduce our reliance on fossil fuels. That’s why I introduced legislation to require solar panels <http://sanfrancisco.cbslocal.com/2016/02/26/san-francisco-require-solar-panels-new-buildings/> on new residential and commercial buildings constructed in San Francisco, which the Board of Supervisors unanimously passed. The legislation makes San Francisco the first large city in the country to take this important step. Current state law requires that 15% of roof area on new buildings up to ten stories be “solar ready,” which means that portion of the roof is unshaded by the proposed building itself, and free of obstructions. My legislation requires this 15% of roof space have solar actually installed, taking the form of either solar photovoltaic or solar water panels, both of which supply 100% renewable energy. In a dense, urban environment we need to be smart about how we maximize the use of our space to promote the use of renewable energy and improve our environment <http://www.sfexaminer.com/leading-way-solar-energy/>." "b"]
["" "b"]
["" "b"]
["" "b"]
["New Ballot Measure to Fix Our Broken Street Tree Policy" "b"]
["" "b"]
["Trees are critical for our environment, health, and quality of life, yet for nearly 40 years, San Francisco has failed in funding the basic task of maintaining our urban forest. We now have a chance to correct course and create a vibrant and growing tree canopy for all residents. To do this, I introduced a ballot measure that requires the City to assume responsibility for all street trees <http://www.sfchronicle.com/bayarea/article/SF-Supervisor-Wiener-proposes-parcel-tax-to-pay-7255902.php>  - including tree maintenance, sidewalk damage, and liability - and provides a long-term dedicated funding source to allow the city to do so.  The funding source is a combination of funding from the current city budget - representing what the city has, on average, spent on street trees over the past decade - and a progressive parcel tax of about $29.50 for condo owners, $35 for owners of most single family homes and small apartment buildings, and more for larger commercial buildings.  Property owners should not have to repair broken sidewalks caused by street trees or be liable for any damage caused by these trees. This policy needs to be fixed in a sustainable way." "b"]
["" "b"]
["" "b"]
["" "b"]
["" "b"]
["" "b"]
["Scott recently joined Mission High Students at the 100th anniversary of San Francisco's JROTC program." "b"]
["" "b"]
["Code Enforcement Reform: Making Buildings Safer" "b"]
["" "b"]
["Making our buildings safe and habitable is good for tenants and for our neighborhoods. But our city’s code enforcement process <http://www.ielightsf.com/2015/12/08/opinion-fighting-blighted-properties-with-better-enforcement/> has lacked coordination across departments and been slow to respond to significant problems with buildings, including dilapidated buildings and buildings with significant life safety problems.  To address this, I authored legislation to reform our code enforcement process, strengthen the City’s ability to crack down on serial code violators, and help code violators who want to correct their violations but cannot afford to do so. The Board unanimously passed this legislation <http://www.sfgate.com/bayarea/article/SF-supervisors-tackle-alleged-police-misconduct-7244974.php> a few weeks ago. The legislation will improve accountability to the public, who bear the brunt of living in and among our dilapidated buildings." "b"]
["" "b"]
["" "b"]
["" "b"]
["Best Value Contracting Reform" "b"]
["" "b"]
["I recently introduced legislation to reform San Francisco’s approach to public contract bidding <http://www.sfchronicle.com/bayarea/article/S-F-may-consider-value-not-just-price-when-7454523.php> – legislation to ensure that we receive the best value for our investment. We are making unprecedented infrastructure investments in San Francisco, and taxpayers deserve the best overall value when we spend precious public dollars to pave our streets, renovate our parks, and build our transit systems. Under the current bid award system, only the bid price is considered, with the lowest bidder automatically receiving the contract award. No other factor, including past performance, safety record, or relevant experience is included when awarding bids. This leaves us vulnerable to getting lower quality bids that can result in problematic projects and ultimately higher costs for the public <http://www.sfchronicle.com/bayarea/article/S-F-tries-to-fire-contractor-over-gas-leaks-in-6589761.php>.  My legislation will change that process so that City departments, in addition to considering bid price, can also consider the contractor’s past track record <http://sfappeal.com/2016/03/legislation-would-make-it-harder-for-bad-contractors-to-win-city-contracts/>." "b"]
["" "b"]
["" "b"]
["" "b"]
["Water Conservation: Requiring Submeters in New Construction" "b"]
["" "b"]
["Addressing our structural water shortage requires systemic change in how we think about, use, and conserve water. Currently, individuals who live in multi-unit buildings generally don’t have their own water meters. Without this information on a monthly bill, people may not feel the need to reduce water consumption as they do with electricity, which is already submetered. I’ve introduced legislation to require that submeters be installed <http://kron4.com/2016/03/22/san-francisco-supervisor-scott-wiener-proposes-individual-water-meters-for-all-units-in-new-housing-projects/> in newly constructed, multi-unit residential buildings. Water is not an infinitely-available commodity, and we need to do more to practice better conservation measures." "b"]

["Support for the LGBT Community: Spending Ban and Data Collection" "b"]
["" "b"]
["I recently announced two pieces of legislation to support the LGBT community <http://www.ebar.com/news/article.php?sec=news&article=71470>:" "b"]

["" "b"]
["Travel and Spending Ban to States with Anti-LGBT Hate Laws" "b"]
["" "b"]
["The first ordinance will ban city-sponsored travel to states with LGBT hate laws, codifying Mayor Lee's executive order, and further make San Francisco the first jurisdiction to ban city-funded contracting with companies that are headquartered in these states and to ban purchase of goods and services produced in these states. The ban <http://www.ebar.com/news/article.php?sec=news&article=71470> will apply to recent laws passed in North Carolina and Mississippi." "b"]
["" "b"]
["" "b"]
["" "b"]
["Data Collection" "b"]
["" "b"]
["The second piece of legislation requires City departments to collect data to help improve services and policies to support the LGBT population in San Francisco. The ordinance requires City departments and contractors providing health care and social services to seek, collect, and analyze data concerning the sexual orientation and gender identity of the clients they serve. Clients have the right to not provide the data." "b"]

["Open Source Voting System" "b"]
["" "b"]
["Free and fair elections are one of the bedrock principles of our democracy. We have an opportunity to fund, design, and implement an open source voting system <http://www.sfexaminer.com/public-transparent-voting-system-san-francisco/> that will provide for more a transparent, secure, and publicly viewable elections system. Additionally, a publicly developed system run on commercial off-the shelf hardware can save the city money in the long-term by eliminating the need for expensive, ongoing private vendor contracts. I held a hearing on this issue in March, and am currently working with the Elections Commission and the Department of Elections to secure initial funding in this year’s project to get the project underway.  " "b"]

["Muni Forward Service Improvements Launch" "b"]
[" On April 23rd, Muni Forward rolled out its fourth round of service improvements in just over a year. City-wide, 17 lines will get more frequent service, 10 lines will see expanded service hours, two lines will make new connections to BART, and two new Owl routes are launching. In District 8, residents will directly benefit from a new connection to Glen Park BART on the 35 Eureka! The 35 will also get a boost in frequency, from service every 30 minutes to every 25 minutes in the morning, and every 15 minutes in the evening. All Muni Metro weekend service will also be increased so trains arrive every 10 minutes on Saturday, and every 12 minutes on Sunday, and the 37 Corbett will see more service during the evening commute. In addition, we’re planning two brand new Owl routes along portions of the 48 Quintara-24th St and 44 O’Shaughnessy. The new 48 Owl will provide All Nighter service between Noe Valley and 3rd Street, while the 44 Owl will serve Glen Park BART to the Bayview. Click here <http://muniforward.com/> for more information." "b"]

["Twin Peaks Figure 8 Pilot Redesign" "b"]
[" The Twin Peaks Figure 8 Pilot Redesign seeks to create better connectivity within the Twin Peaks trail system, improve pedestrian and bicycle access, and provide a defined connection to the Bay Area Ridge Trail.  The City is hoping to make significant long-term investments to one of San Francisco’s most popular parks and thank all of you who have attended community meetings and provided your feedback during the last 9 months. The pilot redesign will be implemented this summer using temporary materials and will allow the Project Team to study how these changes affect transportation around the park and adjacent neighborhoods. The pilot would end by May of 2018, allowing for thorough analysis of traffic changes and visitor and resident feedback and development of recommendations for permanent changes. The SFMTA Board of Directors will make a decision on the final proposal for the roadway at that time, and we will keep you informed as the longer term design proposal, with additional features and amenities, moves along.  Please click here <http://sfrecpark.org/project/twin-peaks-figure-8-redesign/> for more information." "b"]

Their goal is open the SF Watershed to Hikers and Cyclists the nature-loving public that this property belongs to. Click here <http://www.openthewatershed.org/]%20for%20more%20information,%20and%20here%20[https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=KiYcTOCzVKs> for more information, and here <https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=KiYcTOCzVKs> for a video where I discuss the benefits of the proposal." [" The Neighborhood Justice Fund RFP process is open to all non-profit 501(c)(3) organizations that wish to implement projects that will enhance public safety, livability and unity in San Francisco’s neighborhoods.  Organizations or community groups seeking to apply that do not have 501(c)(3) status may partner with an eligible organization to serve as their “fiscal agent” for grant purposes. Grants awarded during the 2016 disbursement are for projects to be completed between July 1, 2016 and December 31, 2016. 10 agencies will be awarded up to $3,000. In 2016, the Neighborhood Justice Fund will give priority to projects dedicated to auto burglary prevention and education, human trafficking prevention and education, and community mobilization events. Did anyone in your family apply for a U.S. passport between 1795 and 1925? If they did, you can probably find a copy of their application on Ancestry. The State Department issued more than 1,684,280 passports between 1810 and 1925. ["" "b"]
["This is the final update for the NYC meetup tonight, now that the weekend's" "b"]
["workshop has wrapped and hopefully everyone has joined this mailing list" "b"]
["who's going to (after this, if you'd like further updates on NYC events, please" "b"]
["sign up here <https://groups.google.com/forum/#!forum/overcomingbiasnyc>)." "b"]
["" "b"]
["It also can be a jumping off point for discussing \"Favorite Emotions\"," "b"]
["which'll be our topic tonight, inspired by this blogpost:" "b"]
["" "b"]
["http://agentyduck.blogspot.com/2016/02/favorite-emotions.html" "b"]
["" "b"]
["People have a wide variety of favorite emotions - including \"joy\"," "b"]
["\"satisfaction/contentment\", \"power\", \"transcendent glory\"," "b"]
["\"understanding/insight.\" Reading Brienne's post made me do a few things:" "b"]
["" "b"]
[" •  Think more concretely about what my favorite _are_." "b"]
[" •  Viscerally remember how great they were" "b"]
[" •  Notice that I didn't feel them as often as I'd like" "b"]
[" •  Notice that there were fairly predictable, systemic _reasons_ why I" "b"]
["didn't feel them. My current job/friends/life situation is such that I have" "b"]
["_pretty_good_ emotions a lot of the time, but don't get to experience my" "b"]
["favorites. (In particular, I don't get to experience" "b"]
["" "b"]
["So. The format for this evening will be:" "b"]
["" "b"]
["1) Spend 5-10 minutes thinking about our favorite emotions and how we" "b"]
["experience them" "b"]
["2) Everyone spend a couple minutes describing those emotions and" "b"]
["actions/experiences to the group" "b"]
["3) People can split into smaller groups to either talk/reminisce in more" "b"]
["detail about interesting emotions, OR brainstorm ways to shift their life" "b"]
["such that they experience their favorite emotions more." "b"]
["" "b"]
["TIME:" "b"]
["7:30 PM - 10:00PM" "b"]
["" "b"]
["PLACE:" "b"]
["Solarium House" "b"]
["20 John Street, New York NY 10038" "b"]
["Please ring the buzzer for Apartment 4 to be let in." "b"]

[">> On Tue, Sep 1, 2015 at 1:52 PM, Glenn Davis < <glenn@gdcreative.com>" "h"]
[">> glenn@gdcreative.com> wrote:" "h"]
[">>" "b"]
[">>> \"Discovering secrets\" (kudos to Satvik) is a good process for debugging" "b"]
[">>> difficult problems. (Note that I'm using this process for a different" "b"]
[">>> purpose than Satvik intended and may be butchering it.)" "b"]
[">>>" "b"]
[">>> The process for discovering secrets (Satvik or anyone else, feel free to" "b"]
[">>> correct me) is:" "b"]
[">>> 1. Set a timer (for 10 minutes, say) and write down everything you" "b"]
[">>> observe and/or believe about the problem." "b"]
[">>> 2. Set a timer and write down alternative hypotheses about what might be" "b"]
[">>> going on." "b"]
[">>> 3. Devise tests for plausible hypotheses, and run the tests." "b"]
[">>> 4. Repeat as necessary." "b"]
[">>>" "b"]
[">>> On Tue, Sep 1, 2015 at 4:49 AM imuli <i@imu.li> wrote:" "h"]

[">>>> better, instead of how much you have left to change, the reward curve comes" "b"]
[">>>> out the helpful way." "b"]

Your ability to send invoices containing an IPN payment link and send payments with the Pay Vendor tool will be shut off May 31, 2016. Your customers will still be able to pay invoices through your Pay Link until June 30, 2016. You can also download any IPN payments you receive and review past transactions until June 30, 2016. With this change, we'd like to introduce a new eInvoicing option for you to bill your customers. Customers can still pay you online and will enjoy an updated payment experience. Unfortunately, we are unable to convert your existing IPN account to use with eInvoicing and you will have to sign up for a new Payments account. [">>>>> until now. We plan to start getting some recognizability next week with a" "b"]
[">>>>> couple meetups scheduled in the SF AI group." "b"]
[">>>>> We are building a personal assistant. It is somewhat similar to viv in" "b"]
[">>>>> a sense that it also converts the query into a program, with couple" "b"]
[">>>>> differences:" "b"]
[">>>>> 1. viv creates the entire program in advance, with all the branches" "b"]
[">>>>> and loops. and then executes it. We instead generate each step sequentially" "b"]
[">>>>> and conditioned on results of previous steps. This way if the program needs" "b"]
[">>>>> to branch, the neural network only generates the branch that will be" "b"]
[">>>>> executed." "b"]
[">>>>> 2. we concentrate first on the use case of answering factual" "b"]
[">>>>> questions, as opposed to ordering food or scheduling meetings, so that we" "b"]
[">>>>> enter slightly less crowded market. But we plan to then quickly build the" "b"]
[">>>>> handlers for all the popular VA use cases soon after that." "b"]

["> those installed), and potentially any other packages. The issue will be" "b"]
["> that a version of the Google commons HashFunction class is getting into the" "b"]
["> classpath from another package before the version of the library included" "b"]
["> with the distributedWekaSpark package. Weka uses a shared classpath for all" "b"]
["> packages, which simplifies the implementation of package dependencies but" "b"]
["> can lead to library clashes." "b"]

["My model could also explain why Silicon Valley is obsessed with youth," "b"]
["disruption, moving fast and breaking things.  It's not so much that young" "b"]
["people have better ideas than old people (" "b"]
["http://www.overcomingbias.com/2015/02/aged-profs-vices-virtues.html), that" "b"]
["breaking things is fine, or that disruption is always necessary.  Rather," "b"]
["we already have institutions (like universities) that are optimized for" "b"]
["picking up intellectual gains by older researchers who don't feel a strong" "b"]
["need to disrupt the status quo.  Like an investor that buys a stock because" "b"]
["it's underpriced, Silicon Valley goes after ideas/research methods/etc. that" "b"]
["are undervalued by established institutions.  It so happens that the values" "b"]
["of established institutions are antithetical to the ones you want for software" "b"]
["development, so that's what SV does best: http://www.paulgraham.com/usa.html" "b"]
["" "b"]
["On Thu, Feb 4, 2016 at 8:14 PM, John Maxwell <notifyjohn@gmail.com> wrote:" "h"]
["" "b"]
["> I noticed that the original article does not mention that CFAR has" "b"]
["> eminent psychologists Keith Stanovich & Paul Slovic as advisors.  It" "b"]
["> doesn't seem that the reporter got a chance to talk to Dan Keys, who left" "b"]
["> Cornell's psychology department to work with CFAR, and based on my" "b"]
["> recollection of a conversation with him, is more excited about CFAR's" "b"]
["> approach to psychology research than Cornell's.  Bringing up stuff like this" "b"]
["> with reporters seems like obvious low-hanging fruit in improving CFAR's" "b"]
["> institutional cred--and based on the comments on the article, we could" "b"]
["> use it." "b"]
[">" "b"]
["> Reading the NYT article comments is the sort of thing that helps me" "b"]
["> realize why academia is so affiliation-obsessed.  Universities are" "b"]
["> basically the most workable model nerds have found thus far for seeming" "b"]
["> cool to the mainstream.  The trick is instead of emphasizing individual" "b"]
["> nerds, who are often socially awkward & poorly dressed, you focus on nerd" "b"]
["> institutions that affiliate themselves with the hard-won" "b"]
["> lifetime accomplishments of many generations of nerds.  That's the reason" "b"]
["> institutions like UC Berkeley are so obnoxious about flaunting the number" "b"]
["> of Nobel Prize winners they have on staff or how many chemical elements" "b"]
["> were discovered there--a university's brand is basically all it has.  The" "b"]
["> oldest college in the US is also the most prestigious (Harvard)--it's" "b"]
["> had the longest time to accumulate institutional cred, plus" "b"]
["> https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Matthew_effect" "b"]
[">" "b"]
["> In the long term, I expect there are two paths for CFAR: the upward spiral" "b"]
["> where their affiliations with cool people improve their brand and" "b"]
["> encourage more cool people to affiliate with them, or the downward spiral" "b"]
["> where hits to their brand make cool people less willing to affiliate with them," "b"]
["> which means their brand takes even more hits:" "b"]
["> http://slatestarcodex.com/2015/08/15/my-id-on-defensiveness/  Use your" "b"]
["> affiliations or lose them." "b"]
[">" "b"]

["I would be interested in, say, 20 people trying out Critch's method for" "b"]
["diagnosing micronutrient deficiencies (" "b"]
["http://acritch.com/bayes-1/#more-2028 ). I think that would provide useful" "b"]
["info about it as a method (does everyone find one thing matters to them and" "b"]
["nothing else? etc.) and possibly make 20 people better off. In general, a" "b"]
["commitment to replicate these sorts of experiments (even if you don't get" "b"]
["super excited by them) would be useful as a check and to cut against the" "b"]
["selection effect." "b"]
["" "b"]
["One thing that I've thought is a great way to get a bunch of academic cred" "b"]
["is to basically be a machine learning / statistics consultant for a lot of" "b"]
["different research groups. (There are a bunch of papers that I've read" "b"]
["where they collected the data, did a dumb thing, and published; you could" "b"]
["reanalyze with a smart thing, and possibly publish it again, or do another" "b"]
["extension, and so on.) I haven't gone down this route because I'm not" "b"]
["optimizing for academic cred, but it seems like the sort of 'making use of" "b"]
["statistics / AI knowledge and specialization of labor' that rationalists" "b"]
["could be good at." "b"]
["" "b"]
["I would think that most rationality applications are better suited to" "b"]
["industry than academia. It seems to me that the alum community probably" "b"]
["already optimizes for this fairly well, but it may be worth thinking about" "b"]
["in a more systematic way." "b"]
["" "b"]
["On Tue, Feb 23, 2016 at 8:04 PM, Alyssa Vance <alyssamvance@gmail.com>" "h"]
["wrote:" "h"]
["" "b"]
["> But how would anyone know if they were right? It's so incredibly easy to" "b"]
["> fool yourself. There's a guy some of us know named Geoff Anders; he" "b"]
["> invented his own theory of psychology called Connection Theory, tested it" "b"]
["> on himself, and concluded that this was \"very strong evidence\" and \"no" "b"]
["> other existing psychological theory has anything close to this degree of" "b"]
["> predictive power\" (" "b"]
["> http://rationalconspiracy.com/2014/04/22/the-problem-with-connection-theory/)." "b"]

["> contradictory) versions of Connection Theory?" "b"]

["> On Tue, Feb 23, 2016 at 5:51 PM, Qiaochu Yuan <qchu@math.berkeley.edu>" "h"]
["> wrote:" "h"]
[">" "b"]
[">> Especially for CFAR alumni, a major application of rationality tools is" "b"]
[">> finding out new truths about *yourself*, like \"I have a Vitamin D" "b"]
[">> deficiency\" or \"I hate my job and should probably quit.\" This sometimes has" "b"]
[">> something to do with science in the academic sense (e.g. learning about" "b"]
[">> which vitamin deficiencies are important and likely) but it's something" "b"]
[">> that anyone can try to practice and get better at without finding out new" "b"]
[">> truths about *everybody*." "b"]
[">>" "b"]
[">> On Tue, Feb 23, 2016 at 5:44 PM Alyssa Vance <alyssamvance@gmail.com>" "h"]
[">> wrote:" "h"]
[">>" "b"]
[">>> I think we might be going about this \"rationality\" thing all wrong." "b"]
[">>>" "b"]
[">>> Having true beliefs is useful, and there's many cases where it's hard" "b"]
[">>> for human brainware to reach true beliefs. Hence, we build tools like" "b"]
[">>> \"scholarship\", \"science\", \"rationality\", and \"skepticism\" to make it" "b"]
[">>> easier. Similarly, humans are bad at programming, so we build tools called" "b"]
[">>> \"programming languages\", instead of working directly with machine code." "b"]
[">>>" "b"]
[">>> But, in general, tools have to be developed together with specific" "b"]
[">>> applications of those tools. I love programming in Clojure, but Clojure is" "b"]
[">>> only good because people built lots of software in it - the experience of" "b"]
[">>> making complex programs told Rich Hickey, the inventor, which parts he had" "b"]
[">>> to fix. If Hickey came up with ideas in a vacuum, and used them to make" "b"]
[">>> Clojure without using Clojure to build real programs, the result would" "b"]
[">>> probably suck." "b"]
[">>>" "b"]
[">>> Similarly, tools for truth-finding need to be tested and refined by" "b"]
[">>> using them to find truths - used in anger, as my friend Crutcher says." "b"]
[">>> You'd get suspicious if your friend Bob said everyone liked a new" "b"]
[">>> programming language, but most of the people recommending it weren't" "b"]
[">>> programmers; or if he talked about how great some mountain-climbing gear" "b"]
[">>> was, but most people who bought it didn't climb mountains; or if he" "b"]
[">>> recommended a new SUV, but most of its owners never went off-road (these" "b"]
[">>> are all real examples, actually). As far as I can tell, most people" "b"]
[">>> interested in CFAR aren't becoming scientists - not just in the narrow" "b"]
[">>> academic sense, although that's part of it, but in the sense of applying" "b"]
[">>> lots of effort to using evidence to uncover important new facts. How can" "b"]
[">>> one, realistically speaking, build new fact-finding tools without finding" "b"]
[">>> any new facts?" "b"]
[">>>" "b"]
[">>> This is speculative, but here are some ideas for things we could do here:" "b"]
[">>>" "b"]
[">>>  - Partner with science-reform organizations; try to get journals to end" "b"]
[">>> P-value hacking, require pre-registration of studies, publish raw data," "b"]
[">>> remove paywalls, and so on. We can also probably think of more" "b"]
[">>> recommendations which haven't been widely discussed yet." "b"]
[">>>" "b"]
[">>>  - Try to develop alternatives to standard academic journals. Eliezer is" "b"]
[">>> trying with Arbital, but I expect we'd need many attempts here before we" "b"]
[">>> can expect one major success." "b"]
[">>>" "b"]
[">>>  - Try to develop fields that aren't well-covered by traditional" "b"]
[">>> academia. In particular, futurology (in the most general sense, not just AI" "b"]
[">>> risk) has been almost entirely abandoned, by both academia and by popular" "b"]
[">>> proponents like Kurzweil." "b"]
[">>>" "b"]
[">>> --" "b"]
[">>> - Alyssa" "b"]

["" "b"]
["> For one, negative self-reinforcement feels icky to me. Some suspicion" "b"]
["> that, when I do that, I'm doing some psychological damage of some sort," "b"]
["> though I'm uncertain I could explain exactly what." "b"]
[">" "b"]
["> Moreover, positive and negative reinforcement reinforce their entire" "b"]
["> training context, and not just the target. Thus, when you use reinforcement" "b"]
["> on yourself, you're also training you to train yourself (in positive" "b"]
["> reinforcement) or not (in negative reinforcement). If you want to keep" "b"]
["> training yourself, a program of mostly negative self-reinforcement will" "b"]
["> fIzzle over time, while a program of mostly positive self-reinforcement" "b"]
["> should make itself stronger." "b"]

["One: re: silly toothbrush designs, movies, etc. One of the biggest gestalt" "b"]
["differences between my memories of \"conversations in rationality community\"" "b"]
["and \"conversations outside rationality community\" is the relative" "b"]
["concentration of *absurdity/silliness *in the conversation. I love" "b"]
["sometimes talking about absurd things, because life is ridiculous. I" "b"]
["*love *getting" "b"]
["shit done and learning new things and figuring stuff out, but so many of" "b"]
["the happiest conversations I've had seemed to be defined by \"this" "b"]
["conversation has no external goal\": I'm not trying to learn something about" "b"]
["science, I'm not trying to solve a problem, I'm not trying to improve the" "b"]
["world, etc. I'm just talking with someone I like, about the hilarity and" "b"]
["weirdness and joy and roughness and wonder of being a human being." "b"]
["" "b"]
["Two: Qiaochu's comment made me laugh out loud, but also nod in solemn" "b"]
["agreement. At times in my interactions with people from the rationality" "b"]
["community I've thought something along the lines of \"I wish everyone would" "b"]
["just lighten up\": I'd like to not think about whether I'm saying something" "b"]
["smart, about whether I'm finding the lowest hanging fruit for a problem I'm" "b"]
["facing, about whether I'm living or working optimally. I'd like to just" "b"]
["share things about myself, learn things about the other person, crack" "b"]
["jokes, share stories." "b"]
["" "b"]
["Three: *Conversely,* often when I hang out with my closest friends from" "b"]
["college or medical school, we have a *hell *of a time together, but there" "b"]
["are moments I wish we would talk more about actually saving the world," "b"]
["solving big problems, becoming more effective people :) I enjoy the mixture" "b"]
["of topics a lot." "b"]
["" "b"]
["Four: could this issue be something that's elusive to solve by working on" "b"]
["it directly? I can see people from this community saying \"There's a problem" "b"]
["here, let's fix it by doing X and Y!\" when my pessimistic side says \"This" "b"]
["is exactly the sort of problem that can't be solved by agent-iness, it just" "b"]
["has to *happen*.\" I think I may be wrong though. Obviously, meaningful," "b"]
["lasting friendships can't be *made*; but perhaps we could try new things /" "b"]
["do new things to increase the chances of them forming." "b"]

[">>>> stereotypical and relevant example is ambition; it's exciting on dates to" "b"]
[">>>> see that this person wants to go somewhere and has the competence to attack" "b"]
[">>>> it, but then once you're dating them you realize they prefer long nights at" "b"]
[">>>> the office to being home with you. Since ambition / growth / tackling big" "b"]

["Hi Elle. I think the arguments for probability theory, why we use it, what" "b"]
["it means to have a 50% probability of something, when a person can" "b"]
["justifiably say that there is a 50% chance of rain, what prerequisites are" "b"]
["required to reach a conclusion of \"50% chance of rain\", etc., are laid out" "b"]
["by Jaynes in Probability Theory: A Logic of Science (" "b"]
["http://bayes.wustl.edu/etj/prob/book.pdf). Several of Jaynes' conclusions" "b"]
["are still controversial, but his work shows that quite a lot of stuff can" "b"]
["be mathematically derived from a few basic assumptions about how to reason" "b"]
["about the world." "b"]

["Hi Oge. Unfortunately, the economics of constructing an efficient data" "b"]
["center tend to be kept highly confidential, because billions are spent on" "b"]
["them and so even a 1% improvement in efficiency can be a significant" "b"]
["competitive advantage. In the case of an em city, I doubt current" "b"]
["construction practices would be of much help anyway. 80% of them would be" "b"]
["made obsolete by future highly advanced robotics and material science, and" "b"]
["the other 80% (the two 80%s overlap) would be made obsolete by not having" "b"]
["flesh-and-blood humans around to demand height restrictions," "b"]
["single-family-residential-only zoning, kickbacks to union bosses," "b"]
["electrical codes that require lots of work by well-connected local" "b"]
["electricians, landscaping requirements, parking requirements, setback" "b"]
["requirements, shadow requirements, bulk requirements, FAR limits and" "b"]
["plumbing codes and septic tanks and disability access and on and on and on." "b"]
["I can say that a huge concern will be power" "b"]
["generation/distribution/consumption and heat dissipation, and a lot of the" "b"]
["engineering work done there may carry over. Basically, you want a very" "b"]
["large powerplant as close as possible - when you transmit power long" "b"]
["distances you need to a) build very thick wires stretching" "b"]
["hundreds/thousands of miles, b) have more transformers to step up/step down" "b"]
["voltages, c) have lots of power turn into waste heat or d) all of the" "b"]
["above, and all the options are very expensive." "b"]

["*better to rely solely on new traditions that are still finding their feet" "b"]
["than to also use time-tested ones to get some of our psychological needs" "b"]
["met." "b"]
["" "b"]
["As for how an event like this \"makes us look,\" it's not being widely" "b"]
["publicized enough so far that that seems likely to matter. And I certainly" "b"]
["don't think it shouldn't *happen* just for that reason." "b"]
["" "b"]
["I also notice that you seem once again to overestimate the relevance of \"I" "b"]
["don't personally get anything out of this.\" You are of course welcome to" "b"]
["stay away from any event you don't personally see the point of, but I wish" "b"]
["you'd stop trying to convince the rest of us not to spend time on things we" "b"]
["do value. By all means, pitch your own ideas, but you really don't have to" "b"]
["pit them against others as if the community's interests were a zero-sum" "b"]
["game." "b"]

[">>> religious holidays. It's fun in the moment. I would rather celebrate a" "b"]
[">>> seder than watch TV or play a board game or toss a frisbee. I think most" "b"]
[">>> people are wired to want a certain amount of recreational time, and seders" "b"]
[">>> work for me as recreation. As an added bonus, celebrating holidays help me" "b"]
[">>> bond with people I like, I feel good afterward, I get social support from" "b"]

[">>> applied psychology isn't nearly well-developed enough to accomplish all of" "b"]
[">>> our goals. Just as a 16th-century astronomer might very well want to" "b"]

["A new comment on the post \"Don't Bother Arguing With su3su2u1\" is waiting for your approval" "b"]
["http://rationalconspiracy.com/2015/09/08/dont-bother-arguing-with-su3su2u1/" "b"]
["" "b"]
["Author : AlkalineHume (IP: 131.243.183.123 , MININT-QFO23F6.dhcp.lbl.gov)" "b"]
["E-mail : davidkbritt@gmail.com" "b"]
["URL    : " "b"]
["Whois  : http://whois.arin.net/rest/ip/131.243.183.123" "b"]
["Comment: " "b"]
["Background: I am qualified to peer review nanotech publications and have done so many times.  I am a materials scientist who wears a lab-coat almost every day." "b"]
["" "b"]
["I dislike relying on peer review as an unbreakable backstop.  Yes, it's an important step in vetting material, but it isn't the end-all.  As you know, the fact that a belief made it through peer review doesn't make it true.  It also doesn't reflect a general scientific consensus, which is the actual thing you should most often trust.  I can confirm su3su2u1's statement about actual lab-coat wearing materials scientists and what they think of Drexler's nanomachine stuff.  His and my viewpoint on this is not unanimous, but widely held.  So why doesn't it appear in the peer reviewed literature?  From my perspective: why the hell would anyone go to the trouble?  Most materials scientists are too busy doing actual science to spend time publishing untestable opinions about the future of nanotech.  Smalley took the time to do this (and he was an uncharacteristically philosophical materials scientist) in the C&amp;EN column.  Beyond that there isn't much reason to do so.  It won't advance your career.  It's not worth arguing over such unlikely hypotheticals.  So you don't find these refutations in the literature.  Most scientists consider it a matter of opinion (and frankly, it's not bad for your field to take on a mythical status, true or not.  \"Nano\" has gotten sooo much money just for being nano.)." "b"]
["" "b"]
["So a question for you: what is more valuable in shaping your opinion, the fact that no materials scientists have taken time to publish their personal response to Drexler, or the fact that most of them are highly skeptical of his point of view?  Or if this is new information to you, do you consider it relevant to your opinion?" "b"]

["(Responses)\":  " "b"]
["https://docs.google.com/spreadsheets/d/1xq-J5hM1PUYLIo5FHHfNH7F0RcLbGKKxtIl3rjL39YM/notify/show?rev=3&fromRev=3&s=AM5m-fiK6yi3TMpAEpc-9eId9Qdx4Gi0TQ" "b"]

["Open the current version of your Google Document \"Bay Area Less Wrong  " "b"]
["Housing (Responses)\":  " "b"]
["https://docs.google.com/spreadsheets/d/1xq-J5hM1PUYLIo5FHHfNH7F0RcLbGKKxtIl3rjL39YM/edit" "b"]
["" "b"]
["Powered by Google Sheets" "b"]
["---" "b"]
["Want to stop receiving this email?  " "b"]
["https://docs.google.com/spreadsheets/d/1xq-J5hM1PUYLIo5FHHfNH7F0RcLbGKKxtIl3rjL39YM/notifications/unsubscribe" "b"]
["tl;dr:" "b"]
["" "b"]
["Identify as many of the levers that currently reliably move you as " "b"]
["possible.  Once you have the levers, look for ways to remind yourself to " "b"]
["use them, as well as ways to understand their core nature such that you can " "b"]
["find new ones when you build up tolerance or want to graduate past using " "b"]
["levers in the first place." "b"]
["" "b"]
["" "b"]
["Longer version:" "b"]
["" "b"]
["The perspective that I have after (e.g.) watching the Known Universe " "b"]
["<http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=17jymDn0W6U> video, or listening to Tiny " "b"]
["Glowing Screens Part II <http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=1SWZ7qWEjUs>, or " "b"]
["reading about Yehuda <http://www.yudkowsky.net/other/yehuda/> (warning: " "b"]
["very sad), feels to me to be a more \"correct\" perspective.  It's more in " "b"]
["line with how I think the universe actually works, and my thoughts and " "b"]
["actions while in that mode of thinking/being are the ones I'm closest to *fully " "b"]
["endorsing.*  It's like the line in The Silver Chair, when Aslan points out " "b"]
["to Jill that, up on the mountain, the air is clear and her thoughts are " "b"]
["clear, and that once she descends, the air will thicken, and so will her " "b"]
["thinking." "b"]
["" "b"]
["" "b"]
["As a trivial example, I have a very easy time getting frustrated with " "b"]
["people's decisionmaking in traffic, but when I am in this other frame of " "b"]
["mind, I not only *don't* feel frustration—I actively *do* feel " "b"]
["empathy/sympathy/camaraderie." "b"]
["" "b"]
["" "b"]
["Over time, I've built up an explicit list of known levers in my soul.  Some " "b"]
["of them can calm me down if I am, in my own estimation, inappropriately " "b"]
["angry.  Some of them can give me inspiration if my motivation is flagging. " "b"]
[" Some of them help me to be more logical/critical, while others help me to " "b"]
["be more brave.  My phone has been programmed to offer me reminders from " "b"]
["time to time—telling myself \"Remember Matt Schutz\" is a trigger that makes " "b"]
["a very real difference in how my day progresses." "b"]
["" "b"]
["" "b"]
["I find that nearly everyone has a vague sense of a few such levers in their " "b"]
["soul, but that there's a very real difference between \"Oh, yeah, that " "b"]
["resonates,\" and spending a half an hour to lovingly and introspectively " "b"]
["craft the actual list.  Writing them all down (or typing them up, or " "b"]
["sketching them out, whatev) gave me a few very real benefits.  First, I " "b"]
["started to see the common themes between them, such that I am now more " "b"]
["aware of what sorts of things can reliably cause my soul to shift.  Second, " "b"]
["I gained a clearer sense of my toolkit, and can now use them more " "b"]
["consistently.  Third, I learned a lot more about who I am as a person " "b"]
["today, and what I currently believe a \"better version of myself\" looks " "b"]
["like.  Fourth, I got a visceral sense of which levers are most powerful, " "b"]
["which are starting to wear out, and which places have no levers (but could " "b"]
["use one)." "b"]
["" "b"]
["" "b"]
["So my training method would go something like this: do some brainstorming " "b"]
["in a single session, or \"cast your net\" over the course of a week or two. " "b"]
[" Then create a real list.  Then form some kind of plan (reminders, TAPs, " "b"]
["etc.) for remembering to use these levers when they're most valuable.  Then " "b"]
["set yourself a time to check back in after a couple of weeks, to see if " "b"]
["this was useful or stuck. " "b"]
["" "b"]
["" "b"]
["On Friday, September 25, 2015 at 4:44:43 PM UTC-7, Valentine wrote:" "h"]
[">" "b"]
["> Hi all!" "b"]
[">" "b"]
["> TL;DR:" "b"]
[">" "b"]
["> Identify some procedural knowledge that you suspect those training in the " "b"]
["> Art need for their training. Write a declarative model here in the dojo " "b"]
["> mailing list, and ideally also a hypothetical way of conveying the " "b"]
["> procedural knowledge (i.e., a form of training/practice/play). As others " "b"]
["> share theirs, try to assume there's something meaningful for you to learn, " "b"]
["> and try to find it." "b"]
[">" "b"]
[">" "b"]
[">" "b"]
["> Longer version:" "b"]
[">" "b"]
["> Tsuyoku Naritai " "b"]
["> <http://lesswrong.com/lw/h8/tsuyoku_naritai_i_want_to_become_stronger/>. " "b"]
["> I want to become better today than I was yesterday, and better tomorrow " "b"]
["> than I am today. (That's borrowed from Duncan's parkour mantra, by the way.)" "b"]
[">" "b"]
["> One major challenge to this is that some " "b"]
["> <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Introspection_illusion> metacognitive " "b"]
["> <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bias_blind_spot> blindnesses " "b"]
["> <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Actor%E2%80%93observer_asymmetry> both (a) " "b"]
["> cause me to miss things about how I think and also (b) cause me to think " "b"]
["> that the answer to the query \"Am I missing things about how I think?\" is " "b"]
["> \"No.\"" "b"]
[">" "b"]
["> I don't know any reliable way out of this trap. In fact, if I *thought* I " "b"]
["> knew a reliable way out of this trap, I would become concerned about what " "b"]
["> active metacognitive error I'd be making harder for me to notice by " "b"]
["> thinking that way." "b"]
[">" "b"]
["> That said, I've caught a few self-reflective mental bugs using a few " "b"]
["> approaches. I'd like to focus on one of these approaches this week: trying " "b"]
["> to see ourselves through the eyes of others." "b"]
[">" "b"]
["> This takes advantage of the impression we can have that we sometimes see " "b"]
["> others' thinking errors more clearly than they do. This means that others " "b"]
["> probably have that impression about us, and some of those impressions are " "b"]
["> probably right. We don't get to know how many, and we certainly don't get " "b"]
["> to know which ones! But in the spirit of Tsuyoku Naritai, there's a " "b"]
["> wonderful opportunity here. We just have to learn how to listen for hints " "b"]
["> of this from others." "b"]
[">" "b"]
["> That's tricky, though. People pointing at our metacognitive blindspots " "b"]
["> looks just like people being wrong. And sometimes they're just wrong!" "b"]
[">" "b"]
["> One approach I've had some success with here is this: If I have reason to " "b"]
["> think the other person might be hitting on one of my blind spots, then I " "b"]
["> try temporarily *assuming that* they're accurately pointing at a blind " "b"]
["> spot, and try to understand what it is. I view myself from the outside, " "b"]
["> like I'm made of algorithms, and try to understand how the other person is " "b"]
["> modeling my algorithms. I'm not satisfied until I have a clear sense of " "b"]
["> what algorithms the other person sees me as running, and how those " "b"]
["> hypothetical algorithms would produce what they perceive in me." "b"]
[">" "b"]
["> (This is very much like doing PCK research to me, by the way, for those of " "b"]
["> you who know roughly what that looks like.)" "b"]
[">" "b"]
["> But if another approach makes more sense to you, by all means try that one." "b"]
[">" "b"]
["> Also, amongst peers who share the spirit of Tsuyoku Naritai, we have a " "b"]
["> gift to offer: we can help them see themselves by offering what we see of " "b"]
["> them." "b"]
[">" "b"]
["> So, the endeavor this week is to make those offerings to one another, and " "b"]
["> to take advantage of what the others here offer us." "b"]
[">" "b"]
["> Concretely, this looks like noticing a skill or a way of perceiving the " "b"]
["> world that you think those training in the Art of Rationality would do well " "b"]
["> to get better at. Maybe it's because you know it's a weakness in your own " "b"]
["> skills, or maybe it's something you're pretty good at but you think is " "b"]
["> important and non-standard. Either way, the first part of the challenge is " "b"]
["> to identify something fairly specific — less like \"thinking things through\" " "b"]
["> and more like \"have the TAP of `If I feel social pressure, then I'll pause " "b"]
["> and bring the feeling of social pressure to full conscious awareness.'\"" "b"]
[">" "b"]
["> Also, please try to keep it in the spirit of Tsuyoku Naritai: the goal " "b"]
["> isn't to teach *anything* others don't know, but to identify something " "b"]
["> that *helps others become stronger.* I suspect a lot of you could benefit " "b"]
["> from concrete instructions on how to do breathing meditation in the style " "b"]
["> of ki-aikido, but I doubt that's a key step in almost anyone's growth here " "b"]
["> as beisutsuka <http://wiki.lesswrong.com/wiki/Beisutsukai>. But I *do* suspect " "b"]
["> that the thing I've been pointing to as \"yin\" *is* the key limiting step " "b"]
["> for many people, which is one reason why I keep pointing at it." "b"]
[">" "b"]
["> I'd like to nudge us in the direction of highlighting procedural " "b"]
["> knowledge rather than declarative knowledge " "b"]
["> <http://unt.unice.fr/uoh/learn_teach_FL/affiche_theorie.php?id_concept=90&lang=eng&id_theorie=1&id_categorie=3>. " "b"]
["> Because the medium here is written email, I think it's most straightforward " "b"]
["> to give declarative models of the procedural knowledge we think probably " "b"]
["> ought to be part of the Art. But I'd like us to try to work out how to " "b"]
["> convey procedural knowledge, since that's the tricky part and the one that " "b"]
["> will actually impact how we think on a moment-by-moment basis, I think." "b"]
[">" "b"]
["> So, part of the challenge is to *also share a training method* that " "b"]
["> people can try, and that ideally trains the thing you have in mind. It's " "b"]
["> okay if you lack PCK on this; the training method doesn't have to be great. " "b"]
["> It just need to give us something to work with, from which we could start " "b"]
["> collecting PCK. And it also gives us, your audience, some triangulation " "b"]
["> with which we can try to understand what you mean." "b"]
[">" "b"]
["> As others' ideas come in, your challenge switches to *receiving the " "b"]
["> suggestions well*. This is where you pause to notice that these others " "b"]
["> have chosen, among all the things they *could have* emphasized, just this *one " "b"]
["> thing*. So if it seems trivial to you, or silly, or wrong, or very much " "b"]
["> like something you already understand, recognize that *that's what " "b"]
["> metacognitive blindness feels like too*. Try to assume there's something " "b"]
["> to learn from here, and treat it like a puzzle. It's your task to find the " "b"]
["> value." "b"]
[">" "b"]
["> My plan for dojo next week might fluctuate a bit, but the current plan is " "b"]
["> to draw inspiration from what happens here, and possibly (privately) ask " "b"]
["> some individuals if they feel up for running something depending on what I " "b"]
["> think will be best for our collective endeavor." "b"]
[">" "b"]
["> Cheers," "b"]
["> ~Valentine" "b"]
[">" "b"]
["" "b"]

["Why We Are Taking a Neutral Position on Prop C" "b"]
["There's one housing initiative on the June 7th ballot that the SFHAC's Ballot Analysis Committee weighed in on. After extensive discussion, SFHAC decided to take a neutral position on Prop C, which would raise the Inclusionary requirements for market-rate development. While our members support the measure's intent, it's hard to know if it will maximize the production of affordable housing. Frankly, it could result in less. Our blog explains  (http://sfhac.us4.list-manage1.com/track/click?u=c3361c8f451b03fe35d428986&id=8fea65e528&e=1f00e461b5) this (http://sfhac.us4.list-manage.com/track/click?u=c3361c8f451b03fe35d428986&id=800a419339&e=1f00e461b5) , weighing the initiative's pros and cons." "b"]

["Dwellings, Not Displacement in the Mission" "b"]
["Last November, San Francisco voters rejected a ballot measure that would have put a moratorium on any new housing in the Mission that was not 100 percent affordable. In the next two months, almost 1,000 proposed Mission District homes - both market-rate and affordable - will seek Planning Commission approval and they're facing significant opposition. Here's your chance to support building new housing in the Mission. Email the Planning Commission (http://sfhac.us4.list-manage.com/track/click?u=c3361c8f451b03fe35d428986&id=97da935164&e=1f00e461b5) to tell them you want this housing built without delay!" "b"]

["If you have a class attribute set in your data, the PCA filter will ignore the class attribute when the principal components are computed. It will reattach the class values to the transformed data." "b"]

["> > 2016-04-15 20:35 GMT-03:00 Eibe Frank <eibe@waikato.ac.nz>:" "h"]
["> > You should see an improvement out of the box already because the basic MTJ/netlib-java libraries that are included in WEKA 3.8 provide access to Java byte code versions of optimised algorithms that have been translated from Fortran using f2j (http://icl.cs.utk.edu/f2j/)." "b"]
["> >" "b"]
["> > However, staying with Java byte code libraries does not give you maximum speed. For this, you need the native libraries. To get those, install one of" "b"]
["> >" "b"]
["> >   netlibNativeOSX, netlibNativeWindows, or netlibNativeLinux" "b"]
["> >" "b"]
["> > using the WEKA package manager. These packages include native reference libraries that have been pre-compiled for the corresponding OS. Once you have the appropriate WEKA package installed, MTJ/netlib-java will automatically use the native code." "b"]
["> >" "b"]
["> > However, to see really big speed improvements, you will need to provide access to a native library that has been specifically optimized for your system. Mac OS X users are lucky: OS X comes with a system-optimized library so no further work is required. Linux and Windows users need to do some more work. For more information, see" "b"]
["> >" "b"]
["> >   https://github.com/fommil/netlib-java/" "b"]
["> >" "b"]
["> > in the Section on \"Machine Optimised System Libraries? ." "b"]
["> >" "b"]
["> > To recap, the OS-specific WEKA packages netlibNative* listed above include a ?native reference? library that is not optimized for your particular system but does not require any further work for WEKA to be able to use a native implementation. However, these WEKA package also allow you to access a ?native system? library that has been specifically optimized for your system, if it is present. If this is system-optimized library is present and has been appropriately set up, MTJ/netlib-java will automatically use it. Otherwise it will fall back on the ?native reference? library that is included in the netlibNative* package. If that isn?t present either, it will use the Java byte code version that has been translated from Fortran. This Java byte code version is included in the WEKA 3.8 download." "b"]
["> >" "b"]
["> > Cheers," "b"]
["> > Eibe" "b"]
["> >" "b"]

["> > > > If you want a faster PCA, you will have to wait for WEKA 3.8 to come out (and, if you don?t use Mac OS X, you?ll also have to install some native libraries if you want top speed, which can be quite tricky to get to work)." "b"]
["> > > >" "b"]
["> > > > Cheers," "b"]
["> > > > Eibe" "b"]
["> > > >" "b"]
["> > > > > On 12/04/2016, at 4:10 PM, Jovani Souza <jovanisouza5@gmail.com> wrote:" "h"]
["> > > > >" "b"]
["> > > > > I didn't understand, how can I use these two methods combined in weka?" "b"]
["> > > > >" "b"]
["> > > > > 2016-04-12 0:58 GMT-03:00 Eibe Frank <eibe@waikato.ac.nz>:" "h"]
["> > > > > You may have to wait for WEKA 3.8, which will make use of a faster library for matrix algebra (JAMA is replaced by MTJ). This library can make use of native code (if it?s available). WEKA 3.8 should come out soon." "b"]
["> > > > >" "b"]
["> > > > > A fast alternative to PCA is to use RandomProjections." "b"]
["> > > > >" "b"]
["> > > > > Cheers," "b"]
["> > > > > Eibe" "b"]
["> > > > >" "b"]
["> > > > > > On 12/04/2016, at 3:52 PM, Jovani Souza <jovanisouza5@gmail.com> wrote:" "h"]
["> > > > > >" "b"]
["> > > > > > Simply lock program. I can't analyze the new attributes. The error that is mentioned stopping the program." "b"]
["> > > > > >" "b"]
["> > > > > >" "b"]
["> > > > > > 2016-04-12 0:40 GMT-03:00 Eibe Frank <eibe@waikato.ac.nz>:" "h"]
["> > > > > > What kind of error message do you get?" "b"]
["> > > > > >" "b"]
["> > > > > > Cheers," "b"]
["> > > > > > Eibe" "b"]
["> > > > > >" "b"]
["> > > > > > > On 12/04/2016, at 3:28 PM, Jovani Souza <jovanisouza5@gmail.com> wrote:" "h"]
["> > > > > > >" "b"]
["> > > > > > > Cheers Very good, Thank you." "b"]
["> > > > > > >" "b"]
["> > > > > > > One more question, When I use PCA filter to a database with 4500 attributes the process takes, however the Weka gives results with new attributes.But when do the PCA process to a base with 7100 attributes, the program after a 4 hour process gives error. How can I fix this error? I've done the process of increasing the maxheap the weka to -Xmx4000m for example, yet without sucess." "b"]
["> > > > > > >" "b"]
["> > > > > > > Att Jovani Souza" "b"]
["> > > > > > >" "b"]
["> > > > > > > 2016-04-11 19:17 GMT-03:00 Eibe Frank <eibe@waikato.ac.nz>:" "h"]
["> > > > > > > PrincipalComponents in WEKA standardises the data by default, to zero mean and unit variance. There is no need to apply the Standardize (or the Normalize) filter." "b"]
["> > > > > > >" "b"]
["> > > > > > > PCA is mainly a way to help prevent overfitting (if you use it to reduce the dimensionality of the data), or rotate the data so that it can be more easily split using axis-parallel splits in a tree or rule learner. It can also be useful if you have a lot of unlabeled data and not much labeled data, relative to the original dimensionality of your problem (i.e., you can use it for semi-supervised learning)." "b"]
["> > > > > > >" "b"]
["> > > > > > > You could try discretising the data first, before applying PCA, just in case this improves accuracy. PCA forms new attributes that are linear combinations of the input attributes, and discretisation+binarisation+PCA may allow you to identify structure that cannot be identified by PCA in the original data. I?d try both unsupervised and supervised discretization and use whatever gives you better predictive performance." "b"]
["> > > > > > >" "b"]
["> > > > > > > Cheers," "b"]
["> > > > > > > Eibe" "b"]
["> > > > > > >" "b"]
["> > > > > > > > On 12/04/2016, at 9:59 AM, Jovani Souza <jovanisouza5@gmail.com> wrote:" "h"]
["> > > > > > > >" "b"]
["> > > > > > > > Then I read that it takes to process the data before the PCA process. Some speak in discretize and normalize so I do not know what to do. The problem in question is that when I used the process of PCA filter, algorithms classification rates are worse than when made to the original data, because it?" "b"]
["> > > > > > > >" "b"]
["> > > > > > > > 2016-04-11 18:42 GMT-03:00 Eibe Frank <eibe@waikato.ac.nz>:" "b"]
["> > > > > > > > It seems a bit odd to discretise first and then apply PCA. PCA is normally applied to numeric data and the WEKA implementation will actually internally convert nominal attributes into binary numeric attributes. Why not apply PCA to the original data?" "b"]
["> > > > > > > >" "b"]
["> > > > > > > > Cheers," "b"]
["> > > > > > > > Eibe" "b"]
["> > > > > > > >" "b"]
["> > > > > > > > > On 12/04/2016, at 1:59 AM, Jovani Souza <jovanisouza5@gmail.com> wrote:" "h"]

["June 14-15, 2016 |  Detroit, MI" "b"]

["" "b"]
["Toyota, Ford, and General Motors to Present at Battery Chemistries" "b"]
["for Automotive Applications Symposium" "b"]
["" "b"]
["Expansion of electrified vehicles will require batteries with higher" "b"]
["performance and lower cost to support cost-effective vehicles with a" "b"]
["longer range. Electrical energy storage systems must deliver improved" "b"]
["performance and be cost equivalent to conventional internal combustion" "b"]
["engines and permit dramatic reductions in emissions. Advanced" "b"]
["chemistries are critical to achieving these goals and enabling" "b"]
["electrification. Battery Chemistries for Automotive Applications" "b"]
["will bring together representatives from leading automotive OEM" "b"]
["companies, their supply chain, and academic researchers to review," "b"]
["analyze, and discuss technological advances and commercial viability." "b"]
["" "b"]
["Development of Solid Electrolyte for All-Solid-State Battery" "b"]
["Yuki Katoh, Ph.D., Battery AT, Advanced Technology Toyota Motor" "b"]
["Europe NV/SA" "b"]
["The all-solid-state battery is the most promising candidate for future" "b"]
["battery systems, due to the high energy density obtained by" "b"]
["direct-series-stacking of the battery cells. However, the low power of" "b"]
["this system still remains an unsolved issue. It is mainly because of" "b"]
["low ionic conductivity of solid electrolytes. In order to improve the" "b"]
["battery performance, we developed a solid electrolyte based on the" "b"]
["Li10GeP2S12." "b"]
["" "b"]
["On the Importance of Scale-Up" "b"]
["Mohan Karulkar, Ph.D., Battery Research Engineer, Energy Storage" "b"]
["Materials & Strategy, Ford Motor Company" "b"]
["The need for higher energy density in automotive batteries has been" "b"]
["well-demonstrated by USABC long-term EV targets. While many promising" "b"]
["technologies are developed in academia, there exists a gap between" "b"]
["academic and industrial research. This is partly due to the" "b"]
["incompatibility of automotive targets with academic research metrics." "b"]
["However, while some common metrics can be identified, others remain" "b"]
["impossible to translate due to scale. Bench-top experiments are" "b"]
["helpful for identifying promising materials, but key automotive" "b"]
["metrics like volume change are impractical to measure in bench-scale" "b"]
["cells. Thus, resources that enable low-volume scale-up of bench scale" "b"]
["research are critical to truly addressing automotive needs. This talk" "b"]
["will detail various metrics that lend themselves to scale-up, and how" "b"]
["those metrics apply to specific areas of Ford's research, including" "b"]
["sulfur cathodes, solid-state electrolytes, and silicon-based anodes." "b"]
["The need for higher energy density has driven development of promising" "b"]
["bench-scale technologies. However, key automotive metrics and targets" "b"]
["are difficult to evaluate at the bench scale. Thus, resources that" "b"]
["enable low-volume scale-up of promising benchtop research are critical" "b"]
["to addressing automotive needs. This talk will detail strategies for" "b"]
["scale-up of energy storage technologies and associated metrics." "b"]
["" "b"]
["Li-Metal Battery - Application in Automotive" "b"]
["Mei Cai, Ph.D., Technical Fellow & Lab Group Manager, General Motors" "b"]
["Highly emerged EV market evokes the demands on advanced batteries with" "b"]
["high energy density. Among all industrial areas where advanced" "b"]
["batteries will be applied, the automotive industry has critical" "b"]
["requirements on specific parameters. In this talk we will present the" "b"]
["requirements for future electrical vehicle application and the impact" "b"]
["of Li-metal batteries on the automotive industry. Some concerns and" "b"]
["disadvantages of Li-metal batteries will be also discussed. " "b"]
