["=============================================================================" "b"]
["Topic: YIMBY movement's bigger narratives?" "b"]
["Url: http://groups.google.com/group/SFBArentersfed/t/dcbcb0c10f23a2e3" "b"]
["=============================================================================" "b"]
["" "b"]
["---------- 1 of 1 ----------" "h"]
["From: Alfred <mail@firstcultural.com>" "h"]
["Date: May 15 12:42AM -0700" "h"]
["Url: http://groups.google.com/group/SFBArentersfed/msg/903fe5074dc45" "h"]
["" "b"]
["Hi BARFers" "b"]
["" "b"]
["I think one of the reasons that the YIMBY movement encounters skepticism is" "b"]
["because it currently lacks a greater political narrative.  This makes it" "b"]
["easy to paint us as paid developer shills." "b"]
["" "b"]
["Let's look at classic suburban NIMBYs.  They have narrative of preserving" "b"]
["not just the physical appearance of the city, but also of preserving a way" "b"]
["of life: by stopping development, future generations can grow up with the" "b"]
["same slower paced suburban lifestyle, free from the corrupting influences" "b"]
["of the big city.  Their narrative taps into the classic American small town" "b"]
["ideal that date back to the Jefferson era." "b"]
["" "b"]
["Meanwhile, anti-gentrification NIMBYs also have a narrative: the fight" "b"]
["against new homes for the rich is just one part of the struggle against" "b"]
["capitalism.  They fight for 100% affordable housing as part of a broader" "b"]
["progressive movement towards democratic control of the economy.  Housing is" "b"]
["just one part of it, other parts include worker cooperatives, rent control," "b"]
["municipal electric power, and ending police brutality." "b"]
["" "b"]
["So, what are our grand narratives?   This movement probably will have" "b"]
["many.  Here's mine:" "b"]
["" "b"]
["The YIMBY city is the city of collective growth towards a world that could" "b"]
["be described as libertarianism built on a foundation of socialism." "b"]
["Everyone gets their basic needs (housing, food, health,etc) guaranteed so" "b"]
["they have the ability to do bigger things if they want.  This is paid for" "b"]
["by the stronger economy that comes from deregulating land use." "b"]
["" "b"]
["The basic guarantees serve as a defense against the fast pace of capitalism" "b"]
["or urban life.  You'll always have the opportunity to stay put, and your" "b"]
["community doesn't have to move either." "b"]
["" "b"]
["Newcomers arrive, but rather than displace, they add to your neighborhood." "b"]
["Tiny houses line the center of quiet streets, small businesses operate out" "b"]
["of vans, on street corners, and in garages.  Government invests in large" "b"]
["multi-use universal structures downtown so there's always enough cheap" "b"]
["space for families, businesses, artists, and organizations to rent or buy" "b"]
["parts of." "b"]
["" "b"]
["Let's hear yours!" "b"]
["" "b"]
["Alfred" "b"]
["" "b"]
["-- " "b"]
["~~~  ~~~" "b"]

["To unsubscribe from this group and stop receiving emails from it send an email to SFBArentersfed+unsubscribe@googlegroups.com." "b"]
["+1 on everything you said, catherio." "b"]
["" "b"]
["On Fri, Feb 5, 2016, 8:51 AM catherio <catherio@mit.edu> wrote:" "h"]
["" "b"]
["> The sentiment I'm hearing here is dominated by \"The negative press is" "b"]
["> unjustified. How can we rebut it?\", but I haven't heard anything on this" "b"]
["> list more like \"Honestly, some of this criticism might be valid\". I don't" "b"]
["> want us to immediately assume that negative press is unjustified without" "b"]
["> inspecting it. Here are some things from the article that struck me as" "b"]
["> useful outside perspective on how CFAR, and the broader community, could" "b"]
["> stand to improve:" "b"]
[">" "b"]
["> - \"demographics of the workshop were alarmingly narrow\" <- I'm glad to" "b"]
["> see CFAR focusing on sales/marketing this coming year, for this reason. Of" "b"]
["> course it's important to attract people who are likely to actually enjoy" "b"]
["> the workshop, but I think there are people with related-but-not-identical" "b"]
["> backgrounds who would be a good fit, too (just brainstorming: people from" "b"]
["> a non-technical business/MBA background; scientists who have never heard of" "b"]
["> LW before; community mediators). The participant experience is already" "b"]
["> enriched by the existing level of diversity of attendee perspectives" "b"]
["> (through interesting casual conversations, effective outside insights in" "b"]
["> pair-debugging sessions, etc.), and I think more diversity would be even" "b"]
["> better. I also imagine that collecting different frameworks that" "b"]
["> participants already arrive at CFAR with (books we've read, worldviews we" "b"]
["> have) can inform new curriculum development. Finally, people who are not" "b"]
["> already steeped in related rhetoric likely stand to gain even more" "b"]
["> dramatically from the insights in the workshop than people who are already" "b"]
["> practicing related things, assuming one thing CFAR is trying to do is" "b"]
["> maximize impact on participants." "b"]
["> - \"there was something unsettling about how CFAR focused on superficial" "b"]
["> fixes while overlooking potentially deeper issues\" <- While I definitely" "b"]
["> believe it makes most sense to practice/drill the techniques on bite-sized" "b"]
["> issues like \"laundry\", I also felt the workshop could benefit from" "b"]
["> additional guidance on how to scale up. I don't think scaling up to" "b"]
["> life-decision-sized issues (or deeply-held-belief-sized issues) comes" "b"]
["> automatically, even once bite-sized decisions become routine. Myself, I've" "b"]
["> struggled with how to arrange my thoughts on problems that I feel I can't" "b"]
["> crack in one sitting - how to avoid redoing work I already did every time I" "b"]
["> sit down, while also avoiding the trap where I don't return to" "b"]
["> rethink/reconsider my reasoning from several sittings ago. The CFAR" "b"]
["> techniques are presented as one-sitting insight tools, plus their 5-second" "b"]
["> versions. What might CFAR have to say about longer timescales of" "b"]
["> problem-solving, revisiting problems repeatedly, etc.?" "b"]
["> - \"the lack of privacy or downtime\" / \"nor, so far as I could discern," "b"]
["> did anybody ever leave the house. \"<- The encouraged beach walks in" "b"]
["> November's workshop were hugely helpful in getting some" "b"]
["> nature/space/downtime. I don't remember if those were led by students," "b"]
["> mentors/helpers, or staff. If it isn't already a best practice to give" "b"]
["> participants concrete encouragement/opportunities to leave the house and" "b"]
["> get outside, I'd suggest adding it." "b"]
["> - \"another woman [...] said her commitment to rationality had already led" "b"]
["> to difficulties with her family and friends. (When she mentioned this," "b"]
["> Smith proposed that she make new friends — ones from the rationalist" "b"]
["> community.)\" <- I can't tell from this phrasing whether the advice was to" "b"]
["> make new friends *as well*, or to drop the old friendships, but from" "b"]
["> context it reads as the latter, which I find frightening. Encouraging" "b"]
["> people to drop their outside relationships is one dimension of accused" "b"]
["> \"cultishness\" that I don't endorse at all. (A related tactic is implying" "b"]
["> that their non-rationalist friends are less awesome/enlightened/cool as" "b"]
["> their rationalist friends, which I've actually heard before). If *all*" "b"]
["> your friends are rationalists, then it might become socially risky to" "b"]
["> disagree with the community's prevailing opinions. I don't want to see this" "b"]
["> community fall victim to groupthink for social-safety reasons. I also want" "b"]
["> community members to have robust/diversified social support structures, for" "b"]
["> sake of their own health/happiness." "b"]
[">" "b"]
["> On Friday, February 5, 2016 at 6:19:06 AM UTC-5, notifyjohn wrote:" "h"]
[">>" "b"]
[">> Sorry to dominate this thread, but... It's not hard to set up Google" "b"]

[">> it's worthwhile to argue against people who say things like \"LW is a" "b"]
[">> cult\".  Psychology research has shown that people are much more comfortable" "b"]

[">>>>" "b"]
[">>>> Reading the NYT article comments is the sort of thing that helps me" "b"]
[">>>> realize why academia is so affiliation-obsessed.  Universities are" "b"]
[">>>> basically the most workable model nerds have found thus far for seeming" "b"]
[">>>> cool to the mainstream.  The trick is instead of emphasizing individual" "b"]
[">>>> nerds, who are often socially awkward & poorly dressed, you focus on nerd" "b"]
[">>>> institutions that affiliate themselves with the hard-won" "b"]
[">>>> lifetime accomplishments of many generations of nerds.  That's the reason" "b"]
[">>>> institutions like UC Berkeley are so obnoxious about flaunting the number" "b"]
[">>>> of Nobel Prize winners they have on staff or how many chemical elements" "b"]
[">>>> were discovered there--a university's brand is basically all it has.  The" "b"]
[">>>> oldest college in the US is also the most prestigious (Harvard)--it's" "b"]
[">>>> had the longest time to accumulate institutional cred, plus" "b"]
[">>>> https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Matthew_effect" "b"]
[">>>>" "b"]
[">>>> In the long term, I expect there are two paths for CFAR: the upward" "b"]
[">>>> spiral where their affiliations with cool people improve their brand" "b"]
[">>>> and encourage more cool people to affiliate with them, or the downward" "b"]
[">>>> spiral where hits to their brand make cool people less willing to" "b"]
[">>>> affiliate with them, which means their brand takes even more hits:" "b"]
[">>>> http://slatestarcodex.com/2015/08/15/my-id-on-defensiveness/  Use your" "b"]
[">>>> affiliations or lose them." "b"]

["My favorite way of thinking about emotions is as a cluster of emotional " "b"]
["characteristics. That is, \"angry\" is how you hold your body, how you speak, " "b"]
["the kinds of thoughts you have, the facial expressions you make, the role " "b"]
["people put you in for social situations, and the story that explains why " "b"]
["you're doing things. Doing angry things in one area will pull the other " "b"]
["areas in line in order to present a coherent story." "b"]
["" "b"]
["You can find the result of this model in books like \"The Charisma Myth\". " "b"]
["The book teaches you how to get people to slot you into a particular social " "b"]
["role by suggesting thought patterns, ways of holding your body, ways of " "b"]
["speaking, and types of storytelling." "b"]
["" "b"]
["On Friday, October 9, 2015 at 11:03:40 AM UTC-7, xuenay wrote:" "h"]
[">" "b"]
["> I wrote a quick post on there existing a number of schools of thought that " "b"]
["> teach what might be called a “rationalist” approach to emotions, i.e. " "b"]
["> seeing that your emotional reactions are a map that’s good to distinguish " "b"]
["> from the territory, and which give you tools for both seeing the " "b"]
["> distinction and for evaluating the map-territory correspondence better. " "b"]
["> Figured it would probably be of interest to this list." "b"]

["> You can find it at " "b"]

["Topic: BERKELEY - support for Business License Tax on Residential Rentals?" "b"]
["Url: http://groups.google.com/group/SFBArentersfed/t/840c812b7a96c191" "b"]

["---------- 1 of 6 ----------" "h"]
["From: Diego Aguilar-Canabal <da.canabal@gmail.com>" "h"]
["Date: Nov 10 11:30AM -0800" "h"]
["Url: http://groups.google.com/group/SFBArentersfed/msg/5785090152335" "h"]
["" "b"]
["Hi all," "b"]
["" "b"]
["this item is being discussed at a special meeting of the Berkeley City " "b"]
["Council next week, 11/17. I have a phone chat scheduled with CM Capitelli " "b"]
["to ask for further details about the proposal. If you go here " "b"]
["<http://www.ci.berkeley.ca.us/Clerk/City_Council/2015/11_Nov/City_Council__11-17-2015_-_Special_Meeting_Agenda.aspx>, " "b"]
["click on item 1 and download the PDF (then right-click, \"rotate clockwise\") " "b"]
["there's a pretty nifty presentation on Berkeley's high rents and a proposal " "b"]
["to tax landlord profits. IMHO this is a good way to walk the walk when it " "b"]
["comes to blaming the true profiteers of the housing shortage - not " "b"]
["developers, but landlords! The only downside I see so far is that it needs " "b"]
["a 2/3 vote for the revenue to be earmarked for housing subsidies rather " "b"]
["than going to the general fund, and that's highly unlikely to occur." "b"]
["" "b"]
["Unless CM Capitelli reveals some unheard-of grisly details, I plan on " "b"]
["writing personally in support of the idea. If there's enough support here " "b"]
["we could consider a collective BARF support letter as well. Let me know!" "b"]
["" "b"]
["Diego" "b"]
["" "b"]
["" "b"]
["---------- 2 of 6 ----------" "h"]
["From: rituvohra@gmail.com" "h"]
["Date: Nov 10 02:31PM -0800" "h"]
["Url: http://groups.google.com/group/SFBArentersfed/msg/5822b65039089" "h"]
["" "b"]
["In a rent controlled city and a college town where rental property gets " "b"]
["regularly trashed by the students, what evidence do you have to make your " "b"]
["assertion or is it that you think it is so?" "b"]
["" "b"]
["On Tuesday, November 10, 2015 at 11:30:58 AM UTC-8, Diego Aguilar-Canabal " "h"]
["wrote:" "h"]
["" "b"]
["" "b"]
["---------- 3 of 6 ----------" "h"]
["From: Diego Aguilar-Canabal <da.canabal@gmail.com>" "h"]
["Date: Nov 10 02:42PM -0800" "h"]
["Url: http://groups.google.com/group/SFBArentersfed/msg/582bf8b199b51" "h"]
["" "b"]
["Which assertion are you asking me to clarify?" "b"]
["I think that's an unfair generalization of college students. I live in an" "b"]
["apartment complex with many Cal students who keep a neater pad than mine." "b"]
["But that's based on anecdotal evidence, just like your claim is. It would" "b"]
["be much more difficult and arbitrary to dig up data showing that college" "b"]
["students are *inherently* bad tenants, whereas there is ample data within" "b"]
["the PDF I have linked to showing that landlords have seen increasingly high" "b"]
["profit margins." "b"]
["" "b"]
["" "b"]
["" "b"]
["---------- 4 of 6 ----------" "h"]
["From: Brian Hanlon <hanlonbt@gmail.com>" "h"]
["Date: Nov 10 02:43PM -0800" "h"]
["Url: http://groups.google.com/group/SFBArentersfed/msg/582cf4498007c" "h"]
["" "b"]
["I think the proposal is pretty good, but I wonder if making the fee based" "b"]
["on rental price above median might be better at capturing the value created" "b"]
["by the public." "b"]
["" "b"]
["The current proposals:" "b"]
["" "b"]
["• 1.8% increase (average cost $30 per unit per month) to a total of 2.88%" "b"]
["yields about $4 million annually with proposed exemptions, rising as rents" "b"]
["increase." "b"]
["• 2.8% increase to 3.88% (average cost $45 per unit per month) yields $6" "b"]
["million annually w/proposed exemptions" "b"]
["" "b"]
["My plan might be unnecessarily complicated, but I think it would be best to" "b"]
["charge fees that progressively rise as the rental income exceeds that for" "b"]
["similar rentals. For example, Berkeley could create a map that lists" "b"]
["expected rents for studios, 1BR, 2BR, et al in certain neighborhoods, then" "b"]
["charge landlords a percentage of the difference between expected rents and" "b"]
["rents collected. This percentage would rise as the difference between" "b"]
["expected rents and actual rents rises. This way, landlords with tenants" "b"]
["from say 2005 don't pay the same rate as landlords with new tenants that" "b"]
["pay more than double the rent. It would also discourage (marginally) the" "b"]
["forever upward price pressure on rentals by directing more of the surplus" "b"]
["to public use. Thoughts?" "b"]
["" "b"]
["Brian" "b"]
["" "b"]
["" "b"]
["" "b"]
["---------- 5 of 6 ----------" "h"]
["From: Armand Domalewski <armanddomalewski@gmail.com>" "h"]
["Date: Nov 10 02:45PM -0800" "h"]
["Url: http://groups.google.com/group/SFBArentersfed/msg/582fa151a859d" "h"]
["" "b"]
["Aren't college students ideal rent controlled tenants, actually?" "b"]
["" "b"]
["They only stay for a short time, so you can reset the market rate rapidly," "b"]
["their parents tend to pay their rent so they're not as price sensitive, and" "b"]
["they aren't super picky about quality of housing so you can skimp on" "b"]
["repairs." "b"]
["" "b"]
["On Tue, Nov 10, 2015 at 2:42 PM, Diego Aguilar-Canabal <da.canabal@gmail.com" "h"]
["" "b"]
["-- " "b"]
["Armand D. Domalewski" "b"]
["(925) 212-3562" "b"]
["" "b"]
["" "b"]
["---------- 6 of 6 ----------" "h"]
["From: Diego Aguilar-Canabal <da.canabal@gmail.com>" "h"]
["Date: Nov 10 02:51PM -0800" "h"]
["Url: http://groups.google.com/group/SFBArentersfed/msg/58340160c5609" "h"]
["" "b"]
["Totally agreed - my previous Berkeley landlord was shocked when we asked" "b"]
["him to fix burn-holes on the kitchen counter and make keys for each" "b"]
["separate bedroom door, basically said none of his Cal student residents had" "b"]
["ever asked that before so we should accept the precedent set by their low" "b"]
["expectations. Naturally he demurred once I went to the Rent Board." "b"]
["" "b"]
["Brian, your comments are super helpful and I'll definitely pass them on to" "b"]
["Capitelli. Opponents of new housing like to pull out the red herring that" "b"]

["do coding well. A + B has to spit out C. And there's no bullshit. In any " "b"]
["office, if a manager was to try and get stuff done by being vague, the " "b"]
["engineers would just tell him off. They're analytical straight shooters and " "b"]
["mainly implants that don't proscribe to the many policies of the city. No " "b"]
["city has the business to tell its citizens that their kids don't get free " "b"]
["happy meals at MacDonalds." "b"]
["" "b"]
["*Where you are in your Life*" "b"]
["" "b"]
["Most of the NIMBY's are older folks. Much of the tech diaspora is a younger " "b"]
["generation. The older people likely do vote. The rest are figuring life " "b"]
["out. The dating scene, - will she agree to the next date, will she say yes, " "b"]
["will the kid get into the preferred pre-school??? The day to day challenges " "b"]
["of everyday living and making their exorbitant rents and mortgages. Its a " "b"]
["facet of \"where you are in your life\" I know some of you are fairly young " "b"]
["and heavily involved but many in the tech world are different. " "b"]
["" "b"]
["*The Silicon Valley versus just SF*" "b"]
["" "b"]
["*Th*ey are living the dream of being in SF for a few years but in no terms " "b"]
["seem entitled. They work too much and spend much of their time on the " "b"]
["freeway. Anyone that works starting Redwood City and further south is " "b"]
["commuting an average of 2.5 hours in peak hours and 2 in off -peak. Its as " "b"]
["if all of Silicon valley is a city as a whole and SF almost like the " "b"]
["coolest neighborhood to hang out in. " "b"]
["" "b"]
["*Entitlements*" "b"]
["" "b"]
["Some decide to leave when they find it unaffordable, expensive, crime " "b"]
["-ridden or a city with poor public schools. They don't feel entitled that " "b"]
["they must live in SF and if the cost of living goes up, they will be " "b"]
["displaced. Theirs a simpler philosophy of living a more stress free life " "b"]
["where you can easily park your car to pick your kids up from school and you " "b"]
["don't have to stress over a parking ticket if your hair stylist takes " "b"]
["longer with the blow-dry. So as and when needed they move. The city doesn't " "b"]
["offer them incentives to stay put and modify external surrounding to make " "b"]
["their own. I have plenty of friends that have moved out of SF to the " "b"]
["suburbs to make room for their growing families where the money they funnel " "b"]
["into public schools is traded off by cheaper mortgages or more expensive " "b"]

["Ramon)." "b"]

["The only thing that will help is actively reaching out over and over again " "b"]

["\tRegarding Campos's proposal, I don't know. I'm not a big fan of absentee voting. I always vote in person if I'm in town, and I think there's a lot to be said for doing so. If someone's away on vacation or homebound or whatever, fine, but I don't want to encourage everyone to vote in advance of the election. The longer the ballots are in the hands of city officials before the results are publicly released, the more opportunity there is for malfeasance. If the system were totally open and transparent, and I had a high level of confidence in how ballots are being processed now, I'd be more open to it. But -- see previously raised questions, among others." "b"]

["I'm a MIT student researcher at the Computer Science Artificial" "b"]
["Intelligence Lab working with NLP. I'm currently trying to find a way to" "b"]
["use NLP to parse and aggregate data from cancer research articles to form" "b"]
["comprehensive summaries about a topic (think an automated version of" "b"]
["wikipedia)." "b"]
["" "b"]
["Currently, I'm trying to use NLP to form summaries about a specific" "b"]
["subtopic (diet intake and breast cancer risk). However, ideally, in the far" "b"]
["far future, this algorithm would be able to form summaries about a research" "b"]
["topic, perhaps in response to a specific query." "b"]
["" "b"]
["To this end, I've started working on this issue by running human-written" "b"]
["topic summaries with attached references through a TF-IDF searcher to" "b"]
["reverse engineer what sentences in the source documents were considered" "b"]
["\"important\" by the human summarizer. However, this failed because it looks" "b"]
["like for a given hand-written summary, humans tend to directly cite very" "b"]
["few articles and also add background information (such as cancer" "b"]
["statistics) that could come from any one of hundreds of articles, most" "b"]
["irrelevant to the topic the human is summarizing." "b"]
["" "b"]
["As you can see, I'm having a lot of trouble making headway with this" "b"]
["project for the moment, so any thoughts you have on the subject would be" "b"]
["wonderful! Riley told me that you were working on something similar to this" "b"]
["while at MetaMed..." "b"]

[">>>>" "b"]
[">>>>> Let me throw some ideas here and leave:" "b"]
[">>>>>" "b"]
[">>>>> 1)Some of the problem is just combinatorial explosion, there's too" "b"]
[">>>>> many of us who are too interesting and potential friends, and we don't know" "b"]
[">>>>> what to do about it." "b"]
[">>>>>" "b"]
[">>>>> 2)Some of it is rent. The reason why people can't afford the time to" "b"]
[">>>>> just hang out is frequently because making ends meet where every square" "b"]
[">>>>> inch counts is hard." "b"]
[">>>>>" "b"]
[">>>>> 3)John thanks for the nomination of superconductor, which of course" "b"]
[">>>>> I'll decline because of the Great Project. Although some people do function" "b"]
[">>>>> as conductors in our space (I'm thinking Alton, Jolly, Oli, Malcolm," "b"]
[">>>>> Brayden, me and part of CFAR) I don't actually think that more conductors" "b"]
[">>>>> or one superconductor solves this issue." "b"]
[">>>>>" "b"]
[">>>>> 4)In my personal affairs, I have decided to frequently only undertake" "b"]
[">>>>> activities that fill in two or more needs at the same time. So I'll do" "b"]
[">>>>> something that fills the need for 1feeling accepted, 2for exercise, 3for" "b"]
[">>>>> sensual innuendo and 4for socializing by going to ecstatic dance, and I'll" "b"]
[">>>>> fill the need for 1worldsaving, 2socializing, 3thinking about complex" "b"]
[">>>>> topics and 4having a Visa by discussing Altruism for my PHD paper with a" "b"]
[">>>>> rationalist pal." "b"]
[">>>>> In the same vein, I have opted out of just hanging out, or of building" "b"]
[">>>>> friendships except if there is *also, on top of that*, a hot-tub, or" "b"]
[">>>>> a dating framework, or a skill I need to learn, or an eating-together" "b"]
[">>>>> ritual.    I don't know if I'm unique in that respect, but these days, if" "b"]
[">>>>> an activity can only fill in the loneliness gap, or only fill in the" "b"]
[">>>>> sensation of acceptance, or the sensation of friendliness, I just don't do" "b"]
[">>>>> it. If other people are as crazy as me - and I bet many are - the whole" "b"]
[">>>>> situation becomes complex indeed." "b"]
[">>>>>" "b"]
[">>>>> Here I have laid a bunch of problems and given no solution at all." "b"]
[">>>>>" "b"]
[">>>>> I leave you with a hug and sincere desire that this be solved, while" "b"]
[">>>>> at the same time having a strong suspicion that making the world better by" "b"]
[">>>>> the most effective means possible just plainly require some amount of" "b"]
[">>>>> sub-optimal existential loneliness." "b"]
[">>>>>" "b"]

["> 1. In an attempt to extend beyond Barack/Michele I downloaded the " "b"]
["> BioMed Central Full Corpus of DeepDive-ready DB Dump and am attempting " "b"]
["> to write extractors. I've turned on extra logging, etc.....but was " "b"]
["> wondering first (before I get too far) if the attached file looks " "b"]
["> correct with regard to the 'sentences' originating table after loading " "b"]
["> it from the 31 TSV files. It's 23 GB in PostgreSQL and > 16MM records. " "b"]
["> In comparing spouse to my new project I note that there are variables " "b"]
["> \"ID\" and \"FORM\" in the BioMed corpus that are not in spouse. See " "b"]
["> attached snippet." "b"]
["" "b"]
["I'm not very aware of PoS tags and co. From what I understand of your " "b"]
["snippet, the \"FORM\" attribute seems a little bit redundant with the " "b"]
["\"LEMMA\" one which both seem to be a CVS valid form of your sentence." "b"]
["The \"ID\" field only assigns indexes to each word of your sentence, so " "b"]
["document_id + sentence_id + id allow you identify a specific work in " "b"]
["your full corpus. It doesn't seems to be relevant for your job... In any " "b"]
["case, I think it's a good practice to rename it to something different " "b"]
["(like \"WORK_ID\") to avoid confusion with the DeepDive reserved field \"id\"." "b"]
["" "b"]
[">" "b"]
["> 2. Is there a way to attach an IDE to this beast and be able to walk " "b"]
["> through the Python code line-by-line? Seems like all of my errors have " "b"]
["> to do with Python." "b"]
["" "b"]
["You can try to add at the beginning of your python script the following " "b"]
["line:" "b"]
["" "b"]
["import  pdb;  pdb.set_trace()" "b"]
["" "b"]
["This will pause the execution of the script and let you inspect the " "b"]
["variable values, run line by line etc... I never try it with DeepDive, " "b"]
["but from my point of view there is no reason for they don't work together." "b"]
["If you want more info about PDB (if you don't already know it) see the " "b"]
["doc: https://docs.python.org/2.7/library/pdb.html" "b"]
["" "b"]
[">" "b"]

["Typically, an entire document is processed as a unit, exactly as you said.  If you have an easy way to split the doc into sections or paragraphs, e.g., from XML or clean HTML sources, then you could process at a more fine granularity and retain more structural info about each document for the rest of the pipeline. (Sections/paragraphs can have their down identifier)" "b"]
["" "b"]
["Hope this helps," "b"]
["~Jaeho" "b"]

["   cyber-surveillance bill. The bill encourages companies to monitor users" "b"]
["   and share our personal data with the government, under the guise of" "b"]
["   spotting vaguely-defined \"threat indicators.\" In exchange, companies" "b"]
["   receive legal immunity from existing anti-surveillance laws, eliminating" "b"]
["   user privacy safeguards." "b"]
["" "b"]
["   [1]Call Congress and tell them to stand up for your privacy." "b"]
["" "b"]
["   CISA will do absolutely nothing to protect us from cybersecurity threats." "b"]
["   Security experts say that the bulk data sharing CISA allows actually makes" "b"]
["   it harder to identify real threats by decreasing the signal-to-noise" "b"]
["   ratio." "b"]
["" "b"]
["   Cybersecurity is important, but this is not security. Instead, this is a" "b"]
["   dangerous surveillance bill that allows companies and federal agencies to" "b"]
["   freely share massive amounts of our personal data -- without consequences." "b"]

["Answer from Hillary Clinton" "b"]
["Donald Trump hasn’t backed away from his proposal to ban all Muslims from entering the United States. In fact, he’s doubled down." "b"]
